[1] Prologue
[2] ——Maria——
[3] I have walked this path before.
[4] I think so. No, it feels like it. This is indeed the path I first walked, but I was simply fooled by a common memory illusion.
[5] The width of the hard-packed dirt road, even a car cannot pass. On both sides are endless rows of beech trees, their green canopy covering the sky. The ripe green shade makes one feel the atmosphere of falling leaves early.
[6] It's still September! However, the air in the deep mountains makes one think of the feeling of autumn. The clear air seeps into the shoulders of the sleeveless shirt I'm wearing.
[7] In the scenery that seems familiar, I walk along the summer countryside path. Perhaps this is due to the association with the name Sumiyoshi Valley! The sunlight filtering through the tree tops outlines a dark pattern on the light blue shirt and the exposed arms, and occasionally a pungent grassy smell comes.
[8] Why did I walk alone on this path in a virtual memory?
[9] I don't understand. Because even I, who is actually walking here, cannot determine my destination.
[10] I fled to a very distant place, hundreds of miles away from Tokyo, no, even from Kyoto. I have been continuing my escape route - but if I walk a little further, I should be able to settle down temporarily.
[11] An old friend invited me to stay for two or three days. Their voice over the phone was carefree and cheerful, and it still echoes in my ears.
[12] - Come on, come on! Masaya!
[13] When I asked if I could visit, she gave me this answer, and it filled my chest with warmth.
[14] - Yes, I'll go! I really will!
[15] After confirming that I would go, she smiled, and my expression relaxed as well.
[16] After hanging up the phone in the waiting room at Takamatsu Port, I checked into a hotel near Takamatsu Station.
[17] Since I had eaten dinner early, I had nothing to do with the time. I didn't feel like walking around the unfamiliar streets, so I sat on the bed in the narrow room and stared blankly. After 9 o'clock, I made a brief phone call home and had nothing else to do. Facing the window overlooking the port, I heard the sound of several whistles from the single room, which intensified my loneliness.
[18] I'll see my friend tomorrow! I'm grateful for this.
[19] After turning off the lights and getting into bed, I turned my back to the window, closed my eyes, but like usual, I couldn't fall asleep. I thought the only thing I could do was not open my eyes before falling asleep.
[20] The faces of family in Tokyo, friends in Kyoto, and seniors kept flashing past my eyelids.
[21] As I was reminiscing about these faces that had only just parted, I realized that today was my birthday - the same as the Virgin Mary - September 8th, no, maybe the date had changed. It was the first time in my memory that I had spent my twentieth birthday alone and unceremoniously.
[22] The night stretched on endlessly. I listened to the sound of the horn behind me and wondered if I would ever be able to sleep. The night was so long...
[23] Now, I am walking along the field path in the beech forest.
[24] After getting off the bus, it seemed like I had walked for a while, but it had only been fifteen minutes. The road became a downhill stretch, followed by a left turn.
[25] The village will soon be within reach.
[26] As I think and follow the road, the beech forest disappears along the way.
[27] And at the end of the greenery, there is the village.

[98] Art Village? Sanctuary?
[99] Unveiling the mystery of Kumakogen in Shikoku!
[100] Kumakogen Nozomi, also known as "the wild horse of Tōkyō Stock Exchange" (Tōkyō Tosa), a stockbroker who has escaped from countless battlefield, retired at the age of 65 six years ago, and bought a derelict village in the mountains of Shikoku. Since then, he has been hiding and has declared that he will contribute to the revival of Japanese culture and art in his remaining life. This move shocked the world.
[101] This gentleman, who cared about art and music, was a patron of many artists. He recruited these artists to build a new village and planned to create an art village where they could devote themselves to art creation without distractions.
[102] Initially, the village only had Mukumura and his wife and three artists. After Mukumura's recruitment and word of mouth, the village now has twelve residents, and the artistic fields range from literature to avant-garde dance. These future Picassos and Mozarts enjoy economic protection and dedicate themselves to creating art in a semi-self-sufficient lifestyle.
[103] After Mukumura's death two years ago, his wife, Kiku, inherited his vision and continued to run the village. Since Mukumura's death, there have been many who have shown their talents, such as Nishijima Gen receiving a literary award, Kabe Kouichi's woodcuts receiving praise in the United States, and a solo exhibition in New York. This village, once ridiculed as a "recruiting ground for immature artists," may have reached its harvest season.
[104] From the cover photo of this magazine, one can see the entire Mukumura village, and it is clear from the map that it is located in a remote mountainous area. With an abundance of land in the Shikoku mountains, a remarkable village unexpectedly appeared, causing some trouble to the neighboring village of Sumi. A shrewd character who amassed a fortune through the stock market came with a mysterious group, which was fine, but these people appeared only when they needed daily necessities or to send letters, and otherwise lived a completely isolated life in Mukumura village.
[105] Despite the magazine reporter's persistence, Mukumura village remained inaccessible to outsiders. When we tried to ask for a reason, painter Ono Hiroshi answered, "It is the wish of Mukumura-san and the wish of all the villagers. We should refuse anyone who wants to intrude on the garden we have created."
[106] We believe that our interview was conducted without any negligence, so Mr. Onoe's response was quite unsatisfactory. However, we do not have the authority to enter private property.
[107] Mochi Village's reluctance may stem from some media initially describing it as a "nest for immature artists." Perhaps they refuse to let their insecurities become the subject of their work.
